Many times there is on the head at night a disease which is called "telul", and it grows and becomes great in time, so much that it is visible to behold; and therefore it is necessary that you cut it off at the beginning, and remove all fat, then put on the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays cutting it off until it is great, take heed if it is hard, of foul color, of poor sense: do not touch it with iron for it is an enchanted abscess, for when one cuts it sometimes, great evil comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of gentle touch, not of foul color, and you see that it can be all cut off, then empty the patient and cut off the abscess without fear, and treat the wound with things soothing and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the night is cut off and washed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions of continuation come in one of these joint works, it is of little profit, except for some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is then necessary to do this with anyone who has one, if you look and see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips together with a seam, and care for it until it heals; and if the lips are already detached on one side or the other, it is necessary that you scrape away all the parts of their keratin until they heal, then assemble the two lips together with a seam, and bind it, and powder on top of powder blood of dragon, and broom incense; and put on top of the powders a piece of plaster or another plaster suitable, and leave it alone as long as it is healing itself, then care for it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you bring together the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many men have inside their lips abscesses hard, resembling grains of mustard seeds, and smaller and larger; then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut on each notch, and take out as pincers and cut in each part; then apply a poultice to the wound after the incision with vinegar powder, until the blood is stopped; and then lift off the poultice easily, and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there is on the gums flesh accumulated, which the ancients call "albulus"; it is necessary that you support it with forceps, and cut off at its root, and let the blood or pus flow; then put on the wound vinegar powder, or other drying and constricting powders; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and many times happens, then cut it off again, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, rough and unpleasant scrapings; and sometimes the teeth are black and green and yellow, as far as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; it is necessary that you make the patient sit in your hands, and his teeth be in thy saint, and remove the teeth or the scrapings until there is nothing left; and thus do with the blackness and the greyness, and the yellowness and the other discolorations, as long as they are removed; and if one takes away what is at the first stage, it is good; but if not, one recommences to remove the second day and the third, until you have removed all; and know that teeth need diverse forms of instruments to remove, according to what the work demonstrates, because the scraper with which we remove the teeth has different forms than he with which we remove between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you delay drawing it out as long as you can, for this must not be done; for it is a very high substance just up to the point where one has no excuse for pulling.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is forced to vomit, you must be certain about the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	The patient suffers much from the pain, and thinks it is because of a toothache, and makes them vomit the good tooth; and yet the pain does not depart by this means, until the bad thing comes out, for we have already tried these remedies before; and when you are well certain about the aching tooth, so it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth in every direction with a sharp spatula to ward off the gum from all sides; then move it to your fingers or fine forceps at the first pock and pock, until it is well extracted, then secure the forceps; and have the patient's jaw between your knees, and hold them so that they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth properly without breaking it, and if it does not jump out, then take one of these instruments and insert it inside from each side lightly, and move it as you did initially.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, it should be filled with cloths, there where the perforations are; and if it is strained slightly with forceps, that it does not break when straining; and one must work very skillfully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take good care that you do not break it, and leave one part, and let the tooth regrow in the patient through the evil of the root, causing greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not act like ignorant surgeons who, through their haste and boldness, break the cartilage some times, and do not bring about what we have recounted; but sometimes bring great harm through the roots that remain or through the cartilage they break, as often happens to us; and when the tooth is pulled out, wash the wound with vinegar or oil of sesame; and if blood comes forth, which often occurs, fill the wound with vitriol powder; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, with which one pulls out the teeth first, are those with long pointed tips and large handles, which do not double when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of great strength so that they do not bend at all to the pulling, and be well tempered as iron, and be toothed so that they may hold tightly.
de la racine des dens	Of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root stays at the shoulder, it is necessary that you place a damp cotton poultice on the spot for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the skin is softened, then I put in the forceps called "algefri", by which the head seems like a horn of plenty; and are made inside just like a file, and that's its shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out at all these pincers, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", which is known as a palisade, by which this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the roots jump out because of this, it is good; if not, then help with all instruments, by which the forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument that has two handles, it is thus the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are before in relation to the teeth, and of this instrument which seems like great pincers, it is thus the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is this instrument strong so that it cannot break; and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments which are not counted; and wise and skilled masters find by themselves their own instrument, according to what their works and the disease demonstrate, for there are such diseases where the old did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of cases and one does not break anything or another bone, or if it can be done, then one seeks instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and is aided by gestures; and this is its form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be strong and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but one can hold and remove; and then restore the spot with medicines suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, then reset all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural body shape, and the form is ugly, especially in young girls, it is necessary that you know whether the tooth is born after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot smooth or file it: then draw a line; and if it is uneven with the tooth, then take this instrument which has this form, and it resembles a small beak, and be made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the copes are cut and cut in small pieces over several days because of the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others; and if it appears that one can file it, then file with a similar file like this is its form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth piece by piece over several days gently, so that it does not move until it chooses; then smooth out the end to any rasp, and if the teeth are too sharp and hurt the tongue, it is necessary to file the roughness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front is loose, or by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot press on what they eat without spitting, and you have treated them with restricting medicines, but it doesn't work; then you must restrain them with a thread of gold, for silver sons turn green and perish, but gold never changes; and be the middle thread not too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth aligning, take the thread and put it double between two healthy teeth, then place the key between my teeth, if there are one or more, until you come to a sound tooth on the other side; then resume the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and slowly, until it doesn't move anymore; and be tied at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then tie the ends of the thread to a pair of pincers, and assemble them, and reattach between two healthy teeth, so that it does not wound the tongue; then leave it thus tight as long as it can remain, and if it slips or the threads break, use another thread to hold it in place; it will remain and serve thus for its whole time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of the two healthy teeth and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, then put it back in its place, gradually and carefully, just as we have said; and do not intervene if you are not a wise and skilled person, and one time make the shape of an osseous dent from a whalebone, and put it at the location where there is a defect, and restrain it so that it does not escape, and remain and serve thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the link of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	At no time is this bond that comes from under the tongue or nature, except in one's birth; or by accident of a healed wound; and the works are such that you work on the mouth of the patient, with his head in your healthy state, and lift up the tongue; then tie off the nervous ligament at the large one, until the tongue is freed from its dwelling place, and if there is stiffness or numbness, and this is due to a sudden wound, then put in an unguent and bind the ligament with a bandage; and be sure that the incision is not too deep in front, for the artery that is below; and when you have finished, lift up the head of rose water and vinegar, or cold water, then place under the tongue a linen tent; and wrap the patient's mouth every night, so that the wounds cannot become inflamed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if there is a flow of blood that comes, then put it on the glassy surface and spread it; and if the blood flows, then cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this; then cure him with another treatment until he is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it to be of a foul color or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining into gangrene, and there is moisture, then throw away the unguent, and make a poultice with a subtle spatula, and deliver it from one part to another; and if the blood flows at your work, then put on vitriol powder until it is stained, then return to your work until you have finished all the treatment; then lift the tongue with oil and vinegar, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of throat apostemes
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No growths come within the throat called "godath", and they are properly called the two almond-shaped things; and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then beware: if it is a hard abscess of little sense and dull color, do not touch with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the roots are thick, do not touch with iron, also because of the bleeding; but leave it until it is dry, and then you will part it, or it would break on its own; and if it is of white color and the roots are fine, have your instrument ready to cover, but look first if the abscess has calmed down and is appeased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Have the patient sit in front of the sun, and his cheeks be smooth, and work the mouth and take the tongue between the hands, and press it below all the instrument, for that is the form; and it should be of silver or subtle lead just like sharp knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue all over this instrument, and you see the aposteme, if take hold of it and push it into the amandres, and train it upwards as much as you can; and do nothing with the cloths, then cut to the instrument, so that it is in the form, which seems like some force; and yet the top are curved, and one side another, and are very sharp, and made of iron or andaine:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cut with pincers, so that it is in the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be twisting on one side and the other; and when you have cut one of the amandres, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and warm and gentle, and if there is a flow of blood, gargle the patient with cold water, or cooked grated apples, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it so long as it is sound; and sometimes other apostemes are born in the throat besides the two amandres, so cut them then like the two amandres equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was growing inside her throat, namely the abscess of little sense; and I had already completely closed off her throat so that the woman could not breathe through the constricted passage, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had stayed in such a state for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two canals through the two nostrils of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	Then I hastened, and inserted an onion into one nostril, then the abscess burst open, and it released a great deal of pus; then I reinserted the onion into the other nostril of the nose, and worked the mouth and pressed the tongue; afterwards I inserted the onion into this abscess, and extracted a part, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage in the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing again, and filled up the space I had emptied out, until it became very large; then I incised and cauterized inside the throat: thus it ceased to grow further; and I departed from those parts, and only God knows what happened after me.
de l’uve	of the vein
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When swelling comes down to the eye, and it is swollen and long, so it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is under a lump and rounded, so it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, and you see that the boil abscess is calmed, and it is subtle, so it is necessary to scrape it; and that which is rounded assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of a reddish color or black, so it is necessary to avoid the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, to make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue onto the instrument that we have remembered before this; then insert the lancet into the eye, and remove it below, and scrape with the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the superfluity that is beyond natural limits; for if you cover more, you will harm the voice and speech; and after incision, use what we have said in the incision of two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of being covered, then you should use cunning in the cauterization to dispel their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cauteration is gentle and smooth.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient places their head in your lap, and then presses their tongue to the instrument we have said in the chapter on cautery, and confides with a warm, living heat, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and while using this instrument, which has the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has a beard or hair on their head, put the medicine in it as the hairs of a comb, and place the instrument all over the medicine on the vein; and have the patient sit up straight on their side, so that the saliva and mucous flow from their mouth into the medicine, so that it does not descend to the throat and wound. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the vein for the quantity of half an hour, until you see it numb and the medication's irritation is appeased; and if you see anything, take a cotton cloth and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument into the hollow cane above, until the cotton rises on the vein; and do this many times until the cautery is perfect, then leave it to dry, and wait for three or five days. And if you need to start again with the medicine's cautery, start again, and after the cautery wash around the vein with a cloth dipped in cold water, and cure by gargling as long as it is sound.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take camphor and yarrow and origan and rue and chamomile and vervain and similar herbs, and gather all or some of them in one pot, and put a little water, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glazed with strong earth, and inside the pot have one instrument shaped according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it is of silver or of lead, and whether one of the keys is placed in the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the duct, until the eye is desiccated; after which it often recommences, until the eye dries, and be sure that you do not do this at the beginning of the rising of the abscess hot, for many things happen there; and do not do this but at the declination of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cord and put a hen's quill inside it, so that the patient's mouth does not have too much heat; for the quill of a hen does not let the vapor weigh on the mouth, and it is good care together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Maintes fois s'aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, or aucune chose;
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the top so that they can more easily enter the throat, and have the head lifted high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all come to harm, nor push the bone inside; and see that the patient inserts the instrument, for it is best if he knows what he is doing or if the thing is awkward; so he inserts it downwards, or pulls it far out of all the instruments equally, until it is far.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the snot from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no medicine for sweat, as I have said in the division, by the care of medicines; and when this does not benefit at all, then look into the throat of the patient at the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I told you to.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sweat, so treat it with all small incisions or with fine forceps that are worth this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this is not worth it, take a braided cord, and tie it around the patient's throat, then tie the cord to the bed or bedstead, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full pitcher of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and if the sweat feels the water, then spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not spit as we said, then subfume the patient with assafoetida at the instrument that I said in the fumigation of the ear; do this many times, for it will come out without resistance.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot where it has burning coals, and the pos be covered with a perforated cloth in the middle, and in that hole be the key of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but comes to the sweat; and the sweat will now fall, and if it does not fall, you start the fumigation again many times; and let the patient thirst, and eat salty things and all, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary that she comes forth by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which you treat the snot is this: when you can see it, it resembles curved forceps for inserting into the throat; and it has the appearance of a doctor's beak, and it has a lime-like roughness, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; and behold its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what is remembered hereafter from one and the other in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two manners in which one is itself similar, and due to it holding moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the loose joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the fatty part are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if the abscesses are not to be pierced until the boil is mature according to its fulfillment; and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are hard and do not die according to their fulfillment, just like those that are on joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come in joints, and one leaves it until it is full of pus around it, by chance if the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes constriction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or the abscess is on the principal member, and if you delay perforation until it is mature, then it will harm the principal member; or if it is on the foundation, and one pierces it as soon as it is dead; and it is not necessary that you pierce a hard abscess without digestion being completed, except for the one that is on the foundation, which cannot be drained deep, and will become fistula; and it will not heal in a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to its completion, and this is when the pain is abated, and the departures of fever, and the decrease in pain and redness, and of swelling and inflammation of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where it appears most dependent on the location of the abscess, and where it opens outward; and be the perforation long enough to reach into the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who are bent, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the right place, so it is worth doing that you let the puncture be done until it is confirmed in complete digestion as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you make the perforation before that, then the body will be opened by the venom from it, and will be full of much filth; and by chance harden the lips and deepen the orifices.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the members need it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small incisions for small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many cuts according to the appearance of the grandeur of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut the skin, and cover; when it has become as worn out as a rag, and is exhausted, then it is necessary to do so as one does with babies: and if there are those that are split in three angles, and if there are those who are covered like the leaf of myrtle, such as abscesses of angels; and if there are those where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar covering.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil who have not a head, as aposteme soffre superficial, it is necessary that you pierce calmly; and it is necessary when the apostemes are great, and it has gathered great bowe, and you pierce, if you do not pull out all the bowe in that hour, but pull out part of it; then stop the aposteme just to the next day, then take nothing further from there; do this by degrees as many times as it is necessary until the bowe is gone; likewise if the patient has weak virtue, or women bearing, or small children, or old men decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirits are shaken some times with the issue of the bowe, so that by chance the patient dies, and you do not take care.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, proceed with this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your aposteme, if the wound appears, and look to see if the wound from the aposteme is small; and if it's a clean incision, then try to stuff it with linen or old cotton; and if it's a large abscess, and there are many pits, then it is necessary that you put in each one a tent so they come together against each other; and if you have cut into the aposteme some part of the skin, and you have covered it around, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or raw linen without moisture, and tie it just to the third day; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, then mix cold water and vinegar, and wet the cloth moistly, and place it on the bleeding spot repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, then mix government and care, and the powders that I have said to put in this book, and if it is in winter, and the boil or abscess is very nervous, then it is necessary to place tents and moist cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the boil is fleshy, then it is necessary to place moist cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine, until the third day, as we have said; and then release the abscess and the pus and cure it, as is necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	It is necessary to know universally in treating abscesses: and I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see this chapter.
des soros	of boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or when the boil on the head comes, it is small abscesses that come forth in the manner of threads, just as the yolk of an egg, and there are many similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	It is of fat and such places where there is moisture also like pimples; and if there are such that are hard and stony to cut into, and there is no doubt if the artery does not make contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the cutting is that you test all the instruments which are called "entromissoires", from which the form comes afterward, whatever thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then dry it with the long cloth above.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, then scrape without leaving anything of the peel which contains that moisture, for it comes back again if you leave anything; then plunge cotton in Egyptian oil, if present; if not, in water and vinegar, and apply the dressing to the wound, and let it be until the next day; and those things will cure what is left from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then start the cotton again, just as before, on the second day and the third, until you know well that it does not linger at night; then care for the wound with an ointment as needed, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds no fat, cut it according to this form, from long; and then scrape away all its edges, and strip it of all parts, and put all your care in drawing out what is inside; and if the artery makes a contrary motion, do as I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And similarly, do with the abscess if it is pitted, and cutting and curing as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on top of the pitted abscess and the moist one, for it is lighter, since they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or heads have no moisture, and among those I found an abscess on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess to be like a dry, rough, and white stone, and could not break it; and if anyone had done anything with it, they would have made as much a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming from the head, greater than those that come to the chief of children and to the roots of ears, let the opening be always at its most dependent place in order for the pus to issue forth; and let the cure be as it is fitting.
des scrophules	of scrofulae
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen at the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and are very bad, and are entangled with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly located within its own region, just like the boil and abscess of the head, as we have said; and similar things to these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are also malignant ones that will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one you see with good disposition to touching, and it looks like the color of the body, and is not inflamed on either side nor does it affect the nerves of the neck or the artery or the duct, and it is not deep; then it is necessary to incise it above, and scrape off each part, and if you need to use the two lips of the cure, do so as we have said in abscesses of the head; and go little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, nor is it necessary to leave a gap too wide, lest your hand escape, and see too far ahead, lest you cut something you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you open the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put in the wound vitriol powder, or some powders that stop bleeding, and apply the wound; and leave it so until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the bleeding has stopped, then return to your work, until you have completed it; and then examine whether there remain any small pustules, if so, cut them open and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if the abscess has a large vein in its root, then it is not necessary to cut open that abscess at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it drop down without harm; then fill the wound with old Egyptian cotton dipped in oil, and then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cover the entire scrophula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, then there will be no remaining superfluity because of the greatness of the scrophula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it and pull tight, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophulas that retain superfluity, burst forth there where it appears to open up; and the bursting is done in the same way as the one previously mentioned, by pulling tight, then administering tentations with ointment and similar things, so that what remains of corruption corrupts; and when the wound is well purged, administer ointment allowing the flesh to be healed, until it is sound.
de squinance	of swelling
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have swelling, it is necessary that the incision of the throat which is called "epiglote" be avoided; and one does not make use of these things for this reason, because all the veins and the plexus of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the plexus, it is necessary to cut the epiglote to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary then, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it under three circles or four with a small incision across, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the incision made by syphilis, not in the cartilage; and those who know how to do this are suitable for the section of the epiglottis because there is no flesh, and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, so it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to all its length, then cuts the leather until it comes to the nape; and avoids the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then closes the abscess, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the vein at the nape which sprouts forth through the broken joint and through the lack of voice; and leaves the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed from which one doubts strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound with care, and sew it all up without cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	I also said that one should not do this just until the throat is completely obstructed, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the fault is about to fail.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then close the epiglote because the patient cannot swallow, and it breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death; and therefore the ancients command to leave the wound open until the illness of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young woman take a knife, and she thrust it into her throat, and cut out part of the channels of the womb; and I was called to cure her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that was issuing from it, and knew well that she had not cut the vein nor guided the flow except for the throat, and the blood was flowing out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and sewed the wound, and cured her until she was healed; and nothing befell the young woman except that she lost her voice, and returned to her normal state; therefore I say that in cutting open the epiglottis there is no need to fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess of a greenish color, and it occurs frequently in women; and there are two kinds: natural, and accidental; or if it is natural, it has no trickery.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is of two kinds, one which resembles fatty tumors, and another kind which is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it should not be worked on without great care in someone who is small, and prove and search all around: if you find it like a fatty tumor, and cannot be reduced by any means, then cut it out, just as one cuts out a fatty tumor, and treat it to the very end, if there is no harm; and search thoroughly, and cure it as needed, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of the flesh.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways are ours, of which I will say all similarities; and now it is necessary that I say the whole difference that is between exit and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that pus is warm and feverish, holding on until the ebullition has passed, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the exit there is no heat or fever or pain, and contains its own sac, which is its proper pouch and is in accordance with the color of the body; and it begins like a kernel, and becomes large; and they are according to two similarities, either fat or moist, and very much in color as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the flesh, that you examine and inquire first through all the instruments that are called "intimate", according to what its form will be or according to the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses from us is that you take or more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your two pokes and pokes until you know that the instruments have pierced the core; then withdraw the inserted instrument, and be careful not to let it burst forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moistness comes forth from the core, regardless of its color, do it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the incision no moisture comes, know that it is fat, so then cut it in crosswise, and take it with pincers, and scrape it lightly from each part and follow the direction where you are leading it to come out safe with the needle; and if you cannot lead it out safely, then lead it by pieces such that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing remains, then the wound returns many times; and if there is only a little left, and the blood grieves you, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders, and hold it in place, and put on things that are hot and soothing for the abscess, and cure it with other remedies until it is healed; and if the wound is great, then cut off both lips of the wound, and cure it by dealing with what remains.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beats against you or another thing is contrary, or if you are in a hurry and apply the liquid of vitriol, and leave it for two days or three, until the wound has purged, and the ebullition of blood subsides; then return to cutting what remains of the flesh.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here is the translation:
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of tumors are many and similar, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and if there are tumors that have two shapes in three manners; and if there are tumors that have three shapes and are in three manners; and if there are tumors that have two shapes and one shape only, and are in three manners; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these instruments are sharpened, and there are some that do not cut much more than from one side, which causes us to scrape the nerves, so that one does not cut the vein or nerve; and among these interfering things are those repulsive responses in fingers, so that the patient is unaware of the opening of abscesses; and they come in three manners: great, small, and medium, as you see; and one only uses them moderately in certain places, such as joints, arms, breasts, and hips, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling a scraper for flutes, according to this form, by which blood is staunched.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed sometimes in the place that heals by cutting open veins and arteries, and sometimes retorted according to this great form;
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Breast milk of some men swells when they begin to be corrupted, as much as it seems like female breasts; and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must know how to proceed according to this form up to 2.g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine inserting a piece of char, then assemble the two lips of the wound at the seam, and care for it until it is healed; and if the breast milk drips down below and is wasted because of its largeness as in women, then cut it into two grooves above, by two similar incisions; so that one holds to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from .b. up to .g.; then scrape off the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about seam and powders, and what is necessary in the care, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not yet fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the dripping of blood, then you should fill the wound with moistened cotton in corrosive oil; and leave it so that it melts away the remaining fat, then care for it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	This abscess that comes from under the armpit is a type of hard scrofula or if it has nodules, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and cure it with ointment suitable for this purpose, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like a scrofula, then cut it as we have said in incisions of scrofula, and if the wound yields pus, then apply cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
