et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Et the manner of work is that you instruct the patient to place his intestine in his hand within the wound, if he can reach it; then be sovined on his neck between your hands, and lift the belly; then set the cure above, and cut all the skin off the coccyx long; then put inside the leathers of the size uncured according to what you need to open the wound, and make it such that the breath can issue; then scrape away the sacrum that is below the skin of the scrotum, until the white sacrum is uncovered from all sides; then put your two fingers in that which instructs the scrotum, between the white sacrum which is below the skin of the egg, and between the second sacrum, and depart what is behind the egg, and between the second sacrum; and then move to the right hand within the cure of the scrotum, and set the white sacrum high on your left hand, and lift the egg to all the sacrum towards the size; and instruct the minister to stretch the egg upwards, and loosen what is behind the tie; and examine with your two fingers if there is any part of the intestine wrapped or covered by the white sacrum, and if you find anything, then put it into the belly below; then take a needle where there are ten threads, and put it in the back part of the sacrum, which is after the skin of the scrotum; after the size, then cut off the hairs that appear from the threads, until there are four threads; then assemble one on top of the other in a cross shape, and tie the sacrum, which we have said is below the skin of the scrotum, with a strong tie of two parts; then wrap the hairs of the threads, and tie them together with two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter inside, lest an aposteme should come to harm; and put the tie above according to the first long tie of that one, and after these two ties leave the sacrum which is below the skin of the scrotum the size of a finger; and then cut in the part that is below the skin of the scrotum, until the breath corrects, and the bowels, as we have said before; then apply moistened wool to oil, and put it into wounds, and apply the tie that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white abscess core that we have said is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of blood decoration.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Because this happens often, and let the bandage remain until it is well for him; and if it delays falling asleep, then rise up with hot water and apply what we have said, until it falls asleep; then treat the wound with another treatment, until he is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	(Note: This appears to be a heading or title, rather than a sentence to translate.)
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this vein I never saw anyone who dared to perform the iron cure.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients say that it is made in the same way as the fig which surrounds the gall bladder, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after cutting above and lightly below; then cut in half, and treat the abscess of those who labor, until the vessels fall; and cure him as we have said, until he is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a growth comes out in the groin, as we have said, and opens up the skin; and none of the intestines come down to the testicles, and if any do, it is little and repairs itself every hour; and yet if it stays too long in this state, the wound or syphac grows, until the intestine comes down; and this happens through the extension of the syphac which is in the groin, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and swollen the skin and opens up; and the cure is by cauterization, as we have said before; and sometimes the cure is done with iron in this way: and it is that the patient lies on their back between your hands, then cut the swelling of the growth according to the size of three fingers; and then extract the syphac which is beneath the skin that follows; then take the thread and place it on the visible part of the syphac; and press at the bottom of the belly, then cut the two visible parts of the syphac above the thread, and cut one and the other; then extract the head of the thread, and do not cut the syphac or extend any other thing, as I have made known in the cure of the fig of the intestines; then cure him with the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you dress the wounds, so mend and heal the sore, until it is sound.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The abscess is constricted and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cauterization is more helpful in this wound, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	(Note: This appears to be a heading or title, rather than a sentence to translate.)
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the scrotum becomes soft in some men because the contents inside are softened, and it can be seen; and it is necessary when one wants to treat it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and cuts off the soft skin on top of the natural skin; then assemble the two lips into a seam, and if you see, cut off the excess skin from the softened skin at three or four seams; then cut between the seams, and cure it just like other wounds, until it is completely healed, and the thread bleeds.
dou chastrement	(Note: This appears to be a heading or title, rather than a sentence to translate.)
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that chastisement is ordained in our law, and because it would please me not to speak of it in this book; and there is no need for it except for two reasons: one is that the physician will respond in knowledge when asked, and know the cure; and the other, because we often have need of chastising certain beasts to help us, such as oxen and sheep and goats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that chastisement is done in two ways: or by attraction, or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, we make the beast sit in hot water, until the bowels are softened and relaxed; then we take them up in our hand, until they are restored and you feel them no more.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastrement de taille: instruct yourself to castrate the animal, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cut on each testicle once you have thoroughly skinned them; and leave no small piece or subtle piece that is above the vassels; and this manner of castration is more effective than that which is done by attraction, because in attraction some part of the testicles remains, by which the animal desires lust; then heal the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermafordie is according to two manners in men: one is that between the two testicles appears as well as the figure of a woman's nature, with hair, and sometimes in court it urinates.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has on the finger as well as a member and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Et the cure of the man and woman is that you bind together all the wounds, and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine flows through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the tenia
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tumescence is a wound bound together on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you bind the excess of tumescence to your hand or fingernails, and tie it lightly; and do not go too deep in piercing, lest blood flowing forth come to be, then another treatment follows until they are healed; and at another wound that arises at the mouth of the womb, and swells, and by chance bursts forth, and is according to the likeness of a cow, and therefore the ancients called it "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you cover it, as we have said, with a poultice, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	Of the hare
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is errant if the nature of the woman is not perceived, or if the opening is small; and it occurs by birth or accident caused by disease that has occurred; or it is made in a subtle or sharp manner, and it happens in front, sides, below, or wherever; and prevents conception, childbirth, and possibly having flowers, and knowledge of this is gained through the gaze of a wise woman.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears close by, it tends to occur in the breast or at the side.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle suffumigation, and it appears close to the kidneys, then hurry, and do this: put both your hands on top of each other, and have the woman sit on her back, stretching out her legs; then press the two kidneys firmly until the subtle suffumigation has stopped, and be careful not to make a lump; then take wool, soak it in oil, and place it on the area, and have the woman lie down at home each day, so that she cannot join together.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the abscess is hard and thick, then you must cut it with a spatula similar to a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of flesh-born origin, then suspend it with a ligature and cut it; and have medicines that stay blood, such as aconite, dragon's blood, frankincense, together with many eggs; then administer a cloth made from pounded flax, so that the wound cannot heal; and thus let it be long, and afterwards administer a linen tent; then take care of other cures until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the margin comes flesh-born origin, then it is necessary to cut according to this manner, unless it is enchanted abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the enchanted abscess that is in the margin, one must not touch with fire.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Emorroids are openings of veins that without surgery become accustomed, and when emorroids are old they turn into varicose; and we have said in the division similar things about them, and their signs, and I will say here those that receive a cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and piles, when they are deep within the rectum, and they do not perceive sensation, except by means of iron treatment.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the entrance of the rectum, which one can feel, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold house, then take out the piles with pincers, and cut them at their roots, then powder on medicines that restrain blood, such as aloe and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bathe her feet for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if there is bleeding, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and apply it as a poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it sets, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him sit with poultices on his back and breasts that should not be hurt; then take linen, soak it in juice of plantain or of elderberry with old wine, and place it at the spot.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is settled, then care for the joint with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to a rough head, so it should be covered as I said before with the balsam; and then care for it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Of abscesses of the uterus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come from the mother, such as chancre and stone-like abscesses and herpes and swellings and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary therefore that I say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes to the marriage bed, which is not one of the abscesses that coagulate; and if you wish to know the operation of iron, then look at whether the abscess is sluggish in its beginning, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but let the pain subside as much as possible; and then make the patient sit on a siege, and have two small sieges for them to lean on, and support their back and assemble their feet away from the leg; and be their thighs spread, and put their arms under their knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then place the instrument towards the right side, and administer it so that what enters the instrument comes no deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marris with cloths, so that the instrument does not cause harm; and it is necessary that he puts the horn of the instrument above, and holds the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Et when the abscess opens, and one prepares it with a gentle touch, then it is necessary to cover it with a cloth at the head, at the spatulate part; and when the bowstring is empty, then it is necessary that you put moistened tents in olive oil or green oil into the wound; and place the tent further away from the wound on the bottom of the mare and above the pinioned linen cloth, netted and moistened in water or boiled in mulberry leaves; then cure afterwards two days after anointing according to this, until it is healed; and sometimes lift the mare and the wound by a rinse with water and honey, and then with water or cooked roots of lily and aristolochia longa; then return to the anointing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is set in the mare, then it is necessary that you take care not to cook with iron, but rather heal it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, and she knows the signs when thou seest the woman hasten downward, and desire to deliver her child; then hastens forth the child with great force; then know that this childbirth is according to natural form, and the issue below its head, and the secondine with it; and when thou seest these signs, then it behooves thee to press gently upon her belly, so that the child may come forth soon; for when it descends above its head, then the secondine accompanies it, and the marris of superfluities are cleansed by good purification; and he who comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it happens sometimes above her feet, and comes forth from the body or from the head, or from the hands; or it comes forth from her stomach, or else; and sometimes it is converted by chance upon her neck, and by other bad signs; so it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and to beware of error and deceit; and I will show you all the figures how one must help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out above its head in natural issue, and the woman labors grievously, and her virtues are weak, then make her sit on a stool, or have women hold her; and mix her nature with oil or fenugreek, and then give the midwife to drink between her breasts the little spatula-shaped mixture whose form is this:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	et fende la secondine, and cut the afterbirth, and scrape with one's fingernails until the moistors that are in it are forced; and take hold of the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to purge the woman with a mixture of fenugreek and sesame oil; then let her be pressed and strained again, and keep her mouth and nose for an hour: so now the child will follow.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out too far, then you must gently reinsert them little by little; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up high; then set down the stool on the ground, and hold the woman so she does not stumble; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then cut the hands with the scalpel that was placed beforehand, and extract the infant, and reinsert it evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the exit of the child from its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out of its feet, then it should be pushed up high; and then he turns it little by little, until it is even; then take hold of the feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can it jump just up to the groin, if it is commanded to stretch and make the skin bulge with condiments; if it jumps too far, may God will.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not further as we have said, then turn it piece by piece until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily so.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then take mustard of aloes, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; and put on the natural state of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in cold water up to just below the ribs; and when she is moistened underneath, then give her a mirror's color, and put it underneath, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on the stool, then make her protrude and strain her mouth and nose, and gently grasp her belly, for now the child jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the issue of the child between its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, it puts its hands up and down little by little; then sit down on its back, and let its legs hang down below, and be lying on the bed; and fold its hands up and down little by little, and then grasp its hands on the belly, and take away the pillows underneath, so that it is arranged downwards; and if the child does not cry out, then take its feet and shape them properly, then shape the belly upwards, then put your hands in; and rock the child up and down; and instruct the woman to hold it as long as the child comes.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	Of the issue of the child which comes forth with one arm hanging down
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to engineer a way to return the hand: if one cannot be returned, then make the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her lie down on the bed, and stretch out her legs properly; then administer the poultice that I have described; and if she does not miscarry, then make her sit on a stool, then study how to return the hand; and nurse the child according to its natural shape, and make it swallow, and instruct her to hold it as long as the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Of the issue of the child on its neck, and having spread its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; and when it is equal, so put on the natural muscular power of oil and aloe, as we have said, then command that it move poco by poco; and when you have done this, make it sit on the siege, and command that it take hold; and make it stretch out.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of the same manner for all the secondine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner for all the secondine, so cut the secondine at your fingernail, until the moistors are emptied; and if the infant falls on its face and neck, then cut from the forehead, that it not be held back, and kill the infant; then put the child inside, as long as you have placed it as is fitting, and command the woman to take hold sometimes: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not an unusual thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and do not live anymore if they be named; I know them well, that they multiply and are separated by the yolk which divides them, which is linked to the belly; and sometimes they come out as naturally as all others under, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out easily, then the treatment is as we have said, and be subtle in movement, and do quickly and lightly what it does; and do so that it moves towards salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the uterus I, II, III, IV, V, VI, or VII, or more up to XV, and are all shaped like an infant by the measurement of wise glory, and it is necessary that the doctor knows everything, because similar things happen by chance; so do as it is needed.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman after the stillborn child or in childbirth, as I have said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are constrained to manual labor; so know if the woman is of good health, and has no accident or she fears death; so know that the woman should be supine on her back, and her head inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the minister gives her a poultice of two parts, or it is tied to the bed so that she is not troubled by the descent of the child; then smear the mouth of the mother with moist oils mixed with musk-mallow, althea, fenugreek, and flaxseed, then anoint the patient's hands with these oils and poultices; then put them in the mother's lighter, then choose the place where she puts the pessaries that are suitable for this, and take care if the child is prepared to descend on its head; so fix the pessaries in her eyes or in her neck or in her mouth or in her palate or beneath her beard or in the throat or near the ribs, and if the descent is on feet, then fix or prick and make smooth edges; and it is necessary that you hold the pessary in your right hand, and put a pad between the two hands of your left hand, and tie it all around your hand lightly, and fix the pessary in one of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing.
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then fasten it against the other bone, or the third if you have need of it, so that the extractions are even; and then stretch equally in moving from one side to the other, for the bones to issue forth, and the bones be dentated to hold them, as is the form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if there remains a part, then anoint the ball with some of its own oil and pour it into that part, and draw out the other part; and if nothing remains, then set this bone or higher up, and do so until everything comes forth.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by constraint, then you must wrap a cloth around it, until everything comes out; then cut at the joint of the sole or at the heel, and thus you should do in the other hand, and with both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fue et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fue; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the direction towards the mouth of the womb is also light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	Et si il est éstrois au ventre ou au pis, si convient que tu le estraines à l'enveloppeit sus la main; et fend le ventre ou le pis, tant que les moistors qui i est corrent; et s'il autre membre sont ostoient, et le chiez demeure, si bouche la bail sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusque à la bouche de la marris; puis il boute l'once ou deux, et le traie four; et si la bouche de la marris est retrécie pour apostème chaud qui i est venu, si n'i convient mie travailler, ains convient aménistrer choses moistes et grasses; et l'aménistre emplaustres, et siéce en eau molleifiants et amoistans.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on his side and you can put him straight, then amputate what we have said in a living child; and if not possible, then treat it by parts and leave nothing of the second degree.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the patient brings what we have said about abscesses into the marriage bed; and if bloody discharge comes, it should be washed in cold water, and other treatments applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose womb had borne a stillborn child, then she consulted another one on top of that, and rejected the stillbirth of the other one.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came to her mouth and swelled so much that it burst open, and began great trouble.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the treatment, and I thought for a long time, and could not find a way to heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied ointment of strong attraction, and one bone came out, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very astonished, because the womb has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought that it was the bones of a stillborn child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I sought the wound, and in treating the bones, until the woman was in a better state; and the woman lived long in this way, and occasionally would have a small bowel movement from below; and I remember this chapter only because, when the master finds an unusual thing, he knows how to intervene.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	of returning the joints to their place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the form of the prescriptor, in which we write books; and to two returns for two joints of two lines.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Moreover, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the fist should be one and a half palms wide, and the edge of the trees should be one palm long; and between the two hinges there should be two adjustments of this same wood, which are firmly attached to both ends, about half a palm or slightly longer; and these two adjustments are placed in the mouth of the marriage bed to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, made more subtle and light in its resemblance to pincers; it shall be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of tenaille; and let it have two handles, just as you see, one palm long and two inches wide. And when you view opening the mouth entirely with all the instrument, so make the woman sit on it, her feet pendant and legs spread out, then insert the two handles together into the mouth, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand with all the instrument, just as you have made tenaille equal, according to the quantity that you view opening the mouth of the marris, until the bail does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted and have multiple forms; and when the surgeons have prepared them, the work is done more quickly and the height of men increases according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument that you have not prepared, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained at childbirth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to retain her breath, and then have her exhale gradually, and hold your hands on her mouth and nose; and if she bursts forth because of this, well it is.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, I take the pot, and make a hole or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calament, rue, anise, camomile, cassialigne, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled in water on the fire; then I put a string or hole of the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the womb, and tie it so that the vapors come inside the womb; then let it be done, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine starts quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this treatment and is not completely recovered, instruct the woman to soak her left hand in sesame oil or muscillaige of althea, and then let it return to its natural state, and wait for the second stage; and when she has found it, take hold of it and extend it slowly and correctly so that the womb does not resist the extraction; but it is necessary to move slightly to the right and left, and then pull; and thus it will come out and be delivered.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	Et if the mouth of the marsh is very narrow, we have said the cure of draining, and fumigation with herbs; and if it is none of what we have said, then take care not to do foolishly; but what is in the mouth of the marsh, you must tie to the woman's hip, then cleanse her with a four-drug ointment clister; she will purge and recover, and come forth well; but all the same, when she purges so, it comes to bad odor in the stomach and head, and hurts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore it is necessary to do fumigations that are suitable for this: no ancient has proved the fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain her flowers and secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like seeing a resemblance to a chain, and one puts the head in its natural state, and wide stones on fire; and let there be fumigations above coals, and the lice until they are eaten away, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born without the foundation being pierced, but it is stopped by a small syphac: therefore, at the bath, one must pierce that syphac to its right, and not let it be pierced with spatula-like instrument, and guard the bond so it does not touch; then put on a wet linen cloth in wine and oil, then cure with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not stop, then put a perforation of cloth in the wound, and let it stay for several days, and be removed when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And whenever this stopping of wound or abscess comes, it is necessary to cover that stopping: if it is a wound, then be cured as we have said with the cloth of wool.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules which come from below the fundament are nodation, and grow bigger than those which come from above the fundament to disappear, or in the space of two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when that nodation is old, it works, and brings forth moisture, whitish or subtle blood, and sometimes these fistulas perish; and are known by this, that they either ooze or eject or blow wind when the patient does a bowel movement, and by chance, it jumps out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that pierce just to the bladder, and just to half of the penis; and they reach just to the jointure of the thigh, and just to nothing of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows that the fistula is persisting at the fundament, and not persisting; and it is that you put your thumb on the index or fundament, and insert a thin needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twistiness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twistiness, then I put a thin cloth or the hair of a horse into the fistula, as far as you feel the cloth or hair with your finger; and if you don't feel it, and there is no exit through pertus egestion or wind or voice, just as we have said: know that it does not pierce; and if you hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pushed through to the bladder or to the urethral passage of urine, and the urine leaps forth, and cannot be sewn together by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced just to the jointure of the crotch, then the tendons come just to the place; if there is no curvature and the invention of pain around, then it stays just so, and there is no remedy nor salve by anointing; and in these fistulas Persians have not a cure stronger than labor, and vanity of foolish mirrors that intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In one that is not Persian and is not ancient, there is hope of health by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you lift his legs up to his crotch, and have his crotch inclined towards his belly; then put a tent of earth or a plank if there is curvature, until you know when the tendons come.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the foundation, then you should put your two fingers there, if it senses then that the tendon has been pierced; and be discovered where you feel between your thumb the spleen or flesh, then know that she is Persian; if one does not work at all, then one cannot heal her.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can heal some, but it happens rarely; and the aid that one does there, if it is a subtle cautery as described above, by applying heat to the fistula until it reaches the foundation; and do this two or three times until you know that these burnt parts are charred, which are like a bird's feather; and then cure with moist tents in butter, until those charred parts fall away, then anoint with oil greasing and soothing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is healed thus, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If that is not otherwise possible to be healed; and if the tent intervenes, and does not pierce all the way to the foundation which is at the bottom, and there is a thick covering of char or pus between your finger and the tent; and you see the fistula at the edge of the covering from the heat; then cut off from the beginning of the fistula, and insert it ahead of the tent, and apply the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the top of the tent; and the tent will be freed, and fall away; then remove those burnt parts that resemble a bird's feather, and none will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood flows forth, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine again.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Car the fire cautery assembles two things: it's to know, the burning of joined bones, and the drying of blood and the purging of moisture; then the care of moist tents in butter or in crushed cheese, until the skin sheds water, and the burned bone is issued from the water; then cure the wound of swelling ointments in which hard flesh grows, and are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not come back.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes right to the bottom of the fundament, and is distant from the body, then put your finger or fingers on the fundament, and feel what's inside.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you sense the tent, and between two is the cloth or the wax or bone, where it is close to piercing, if there are no fires except for the way of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three manners: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it down to the bottom, or if you can, put tents and cure it as before; and do not go too deep in front, lest you cover the foundation that holds, and bring forth excretions without volition; then cure it, as we have said; by chance, it will be sound, and you remove that covering and muddy the area around the foundation, either by tent or other appointed instrument; then fill in the hollow bone that is in the wound, as long as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to maintain the fistula in the part beyond the foundation: if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are formed in this manner: and it is when you prick the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the foundation beneath the skin above, so take a pierced tent at the top according to this form.
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put one twisted thread in two, and put the tent all along the thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation inside, then draw out the thread from that perforation, so that you prick your two or foundation; and handle the top of the thread, and assemble the two pieces together, and hold one against the other, and let it stay for a day or two; and then restrain it sometimes, until the threads that are between two come loose and fall out; then cure the wound until it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too far inward.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to make a hole so deep and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spine-like thorn from which one makes a fistula is very rough on one side and notched; and on the other side it is not, therefore one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	bleedings
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorrydes are according to II manners: or they are within the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and great ones, and in court also blood, and there is one or more, and they are further from the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are further have little moisture, and in court also a little yellow water or a little blood, and they have the color of the flesh; and the cure for those who have them within the foundation is that you command the patient to take a bath so as to ease himself into chambers until the foundation comes out, and then the sons appear; if you hasten, and hold it with pincers, or hold it at your fingernail, then cut it in its roots; and if the uncini cannot hold them due to their moistures, take them up by the napkin, or cloth, or a piece of camlet; and draw them out with your hands, then cut them, and powder them with some hot powders that are in place of cautery; or you cauterize them as is said in the chapter of cautery, and cure them with other cures until they are healed; and if the foundation cannot come out, then enema the patient with an astringent and bitter purgative to wash away what is within the foundation, so that it may come out clearly; when the patient takes precautions, and the sons are further from the foundation, then the cure is light; and it is that you take them up by your fingernail or pincers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healed, and he fears the incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit du large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noie le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I pour corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement un drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide qu’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying of the flesh or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times it happens that the flesh dries in the intestine, and through natural constriction, and when the patient is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to cut at the tip of a spatula or on your fingernail the outer layer above which does not let it moisten; then cure it until it becomes solid as is necessary; and if it cannot dry, then begin again with a stronger scratching than before, until it heals completely and is scabbed over; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of the trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A worm is a small abscess located before the breast, and goes quite deep; and often it freezes up tight, and one senses it just like death from numbness, and comes to all parts of the body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a piece of duck quill or strong goose feather, and place it on the abscess, so that the circles of purple pigment surround the abscess entirely; then turn your hand around the entire quill until you encircle the abscess, and push it in deep, and pull out the roots of the abscess.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit, do so with a file of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and drawing above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	but not pierce, to keep the edges together and pressing And if you see fit, then cauterize the abscess, as is written in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the purgative
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a purgative of silver or archaute, or of melted or hammered iron; and sometimes one makes these small and large instruments, according to how they are presented.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore which are presented in the cure of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the purgative, small and great, is thus broad, or the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	et if there is a deviation or the belly is tied, as you see, and the head is pierced from within; and it has on one side two holes, and on the other one; and the belly is filled with medicines from an animal bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around by small holes, and there is between each hole a space of one finger breadth, then fill these holes with a strong thread of crutted wool, in the shape of X or eight, and assemble the belly as a kid; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument before with a strong thread, then cleanse; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg white or something similar, then put it in slightly; then the attendants should press down on both hands together until it is fully inserted, then extract the clyster, and lift up the patient's legs to their full extent, and if the medicine wants to come out, tie it so long as it can; and if the patient sleeps for a whole night afterwards, it is greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you purge him in the disease of windiness of belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then continue purging until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or abscess, so be it that the fissure is as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle fissure on which the skin will be strained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; now we will tell you the cures of hands and medicines, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, and depending on where or what kind of wounds are made, and how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the striking of stone, and cutting with sword and knife or lance or bow or arrow or similar things; or those that are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or on the back, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from the striking of stone or similar things, and the skin is torn and the wound is large, and you suspect lightly of abscess hot: so make it heal quickly with cephalic remedy itself if there is little blood flowing from the wound, and let the healing be on the contrary side of the injured part; and give the patient repletion of wine and thick foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not wish to recover, let his food be reduced, and he should not drink wine or eat meat; and put on the wound, if an aposteme comes there, a moist cloth in olive oil alone, or in vinegar solution; and if there is no hot aposteme, put on the wound all its fresh blood, and it should not be moved by air, powder, as I will say more about later; and if the air has moved it, put on some ointments until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like a cut from a sword and similar things, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together by suturing, just as I will say about wounds of the belly, with suture.
