Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, so lie the patient, as we have said in that who has gilbositeit, and strain I the linen on the sick leg properly, and on the breast also; then put II tisons, one at the head and another at the feet, then stick I tison between the hips of the ailing person in the middle; and be planted with damp cloths around, so that it does not hurt the patient, then stretch each servant towards him, and the mirror place equal to his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If she returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put on the .ie. table, and press it thus as we have said in gilbositeit, and lay the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is before, then it is necessary to extend the affected leg quickly, and according to what I said; and have the surgeon place his hand on the armpit of the patient's affected side, then press with the other hand, and stretch down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the back, it is not good to stretch the patient down or lift him up on the earth, but it should be as if his hips were dislocated at the back, as we have said about the couching of the two hips; and he should lie on his face, and the linen extended as we have said before, and one must press on the jointure at the table; and it will be just right when the patient stretches out his legs, and they are equal; then adjust the hips, and put the poultice, and strain with a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and if he rests for three or four days, then loosen him, and put the poultice on; and if you see they are equal, then stretch again, as before, and leave him for three days; then loosen him, and let him go smoothly, until the member is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and forward, and backward; and it does not dislocate ahead.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	Et li signes si est that thou commandest the patient to bend his leg unto his hip, and if it doth not adjust unto his hip, know that he is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that thou makest the patient sit upright, and stretcheth forth his leg if he can, and place thy back upon his face, and set his foot upon thine; then take hold of his knee with thy hands, and draw it between thy thighs, then bend the two sides of the knee together; and another attendant stretcheth out his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he hath adjusted his leg unto his hip slightly; and apply the plaster thereupon, and make the leg adjust unto the hip, and bind it together firmly for three or four days, then loosen it; and do not trouble the patient to walk, until the members be consoled.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the member is not in place, so administer extension strongly, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes strained and sometimes completely dislocated, and inwardly and outwardly.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tend towards the part where it is dislocated; the repositioning is gentle, and one should stretch it gently with their hands when it is only slightly moved.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is fully repositioned, you should have the patient sit straight, and hold the minister away from the leg above the ankle; then bring the foot to your right hand, and then to your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and push the foot upwards well; and do this two times, as we have said, by pushing and stretching the foot; if it comes back, that's good; if not, you should begin the work again, because it will come back; and if it can't come back in this way, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and place a strap firmly on the ground between his thighs, and tie cloth around, so the patient doesn't get hurt; then hold the minister to the thigh, and another minister stretches the foot to their hands or to a rope that they tie above the ankle of the foot; then stretch each minister evenly, and the straps should be there between the patient's thighs to retain the patient when you're stretching; then put the mirrors equally on the dislocation in your hands, and another minister holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	Et quant elle iert a point, so met the plaster and bandages on it, and tighten them firmly, and bind the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the ankle behind, lest the binding be too tight; then let it stay for two or three days, and if the binding loosens, retighten it; then release it at the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if he goes before that term, it is not certain that it will not relapse again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess appears there, then it is necessary to pacify it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	you must
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two bones are dislocated, then they should be gently stretched without labor, and it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back of the foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a one-foot table exactly straight, and put your foot on what appears to be these joints; then press firmly with your foot until it returns; and when it is even, and there appears nothing, place a two-inch board under the sole of the foot, then tighten it firmly, and let it stay for three days, then release it; and make him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one seeks to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies: if you are not non-presumptuous in the cure, unless you are wise in the art and have used it for a long time, and you are pitiful and merciful and tardy, nor bold; and use gentle things first on abscesses hot, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset now the member to its place, so that the abscess grows cold again; and when the members are at their place, then administer gentle things to abscesses hot, and cure the wound as it is fitting, with drying ointments; and if with dislocation there is a break, and small bones separated, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple illnesses; and beware of entering into a path of fear, according to what I have said, for it will be moved according to your Creator, and by the wisdom of your arm and body.
Amen	Alright is done.
